RATING: 3
The thorn in every deckbuilding game's side is deck-thinning. For the mechanism to work, there must be appropriate risk and reward to building or thinning your deck. 

Unfortunately, Friday is too easily 'solved' by simply thinning your deck as quickly as possible. There are a few rules of thumb you learn pretty easily and then you simply apply the same way every time. 

If you haven't played a lot of Trading Card Games or Dominion, this might be fun for ten plays, but I felt like I worked this out on the second play.

Simple and pure deck-building game, that is a perfect introduction to the genre. Deckbuilders are often criticized for being multiplayer solitaires, but this makes them good solo games.

Since it's a single-mechanic game in which you use all the cards several times per play (except the pirates cards), it's a great game to explore deeper and deeper.

RATING: 8
A small, inexpensive solo game. The idea is that you are Friday, and you are trying to train Robinson Crusoe to get off the island. So you start with a hand of cards that represent Robinson's skills/state of mind. You take two cards off of the encounter deck, and you choose which encounter you want to send Robinson on. Then you flip over the number of cards allowed from that encounter card, and see how Robinson's skill/state of mind value compares to the requirements of the encounter. If you fall short, you can pay a life point to bring out another card and try to succeed, or you can pay the difference in life points, and for each life point you are forced to discard, you can trash a card from your deck. If you pass the encounter, you get to keep the card, which on the lower half is a new Robinson skill/state of mind (representing what he learned from surviving that encounter's adventure). 

There are a lot of factors in play. You need to run through the encounter deck at three different levels. Green (easy), yellow (medium), red (hard). The numeric value required to complete the encounters increases with every increase in difficulty level. So the first time through, you might think it's great to try to fail as many as possible to thin your deck of those bad -1 and 0 value cards, but then you'll have more encounters to face at those increased difficulty levels. Conversely, if you try to win as many encounters in the early round as possible, you may not get to trash as many cards as you like, leaving you with a lot of duds coming out in those harder levels. You also need to consider your life points, as when they run out, you instantly lose the game. So sometimes you fail a lot of encounters and cut cards, then realize you are dangerously low on life. Thankfully, many cards you gain from passing encounters along the way give you special actions, like +1 or +2 life points, +1 or +2 cards, destroy/trash a card, -1 to the encounter's pass level, etc. So those are also a consideration when you decide which encounter to go up against, as you can see at the bottom what skill/state of mind you'll gain from passing. On top of all of this, every time your deck runs out and you need to shuffle your discard pile and cycle through again, you add an aging card, which represents the passage of time on the island and how it wears on Robinson. These are tougher to remove from your deck, as you need to discard two life points to rid of them or use a trashing card. 

If you survive making it through all three difficulty phases of the encounters, you go up against two different pirate ships you must defeat. So essentially, you are not only building a deck to go up against encounters, you are building a deck that will defeat the pirate ships at the end. If you reach the needed level, Robinson makes it off the island. If not, well, he doesn't.

RATING: 8
Very well done! Reading the crappy rulebook, I was prepared to hate this game, but I had a lot of fun playing it. Theme is really comical, although pasted-on, and the art could be a lot better (Crusoe's expressions are almost identical from card to card, which is a shame since this kind of assignment is a wonderful opportunity for artists to have fun with faces). PS: This was my very fist deckbuilding game, and I have to say I will be very curious to try more.

RATING: 7.5
This is a very fun little solo game. One of the best solo games I have played. You feel the theme when you play, even though it is the mechanics that makes it fun.

The only "problem" I have with it (is the same problem as other games of the same type have) is that after you have beaten the game, it's all about maximizing your score. (My top score is 122 points.) To optimize your game and try to find out the best strategy can be fun, but after a while one gets a little tired of this. 

But that said, this is a game I can highly recommend to people that like to play games solo.

RATING: 6.5
Friday is a little clever game I can see myself playing quite a while in the future when I will be in the mood for some solo play!
It's a deck-building game where you start with almost only bad cards in the deck, so the thinning is mandatory. But if you thin too much the aging mechanic will punish you...
The game is very tight, and you can really feel that every choice (and you have many of them, each turn!) is life or death!
Last but not least: somewhat, the theme can be felt while you play (even if the game is an abstract at its chore), and it is not a bad accomplishment for such a little game...

RATING: 7.5
Fun, light, solo game with interesting strategic choices as you transform your deck via it's deck-building mechanism. It'll probably lack longevity once you get used to the puzzle provided, but that's to be expected for a $12 game. This and Space Hulk: Death Angel are my favorite small-box solo games. The rating is capped at a 6.5 or a 7, due to the longevity concerns, but do not let that deter you. It is well worth the money.

*Edit, June 2017: so it's held up better than I expected. I'll give it a small bump, since it continues to be engaging after 10+ plays.

RATING: 8.5
Very much a game of balancing winning the fights (and gaining cards in your deck) and running away (and trimming cards from the deck).  I like the mechanic of Robinson aging and becoming weaker as time goes on, keeps pressure on the player to continually trim the deck, and Robinson feels like he stumbles as he gets older but is definitely stronger on the whole.  Nicely done.  Graphics are quite fun, conveys the feeling that poor Friday the native is burdened with this hapless character that washed up on his beach.  

I found that I'd definitely missed a rule or two my first play, and the game is much more challenging once I used all of the rules.   lol.  Raising my score, I really like this one! (raised my score again - such a great solo game!).

RATING: 8
10 plays: 

Excellent, intense solitaire deck builder. It's like solitaire Dominion, except you win new cards in ever escalating battles instead of purchasing them, and there is a steady flow of cards with negative value that sneak into your deck. Like Dominion, there aren't a ton of options at every choice point, but the simple choices have high stakes and subtle effects. That makes for a light feeling, but deeply satisfying game.

The theme is fun and it's both terrifying and hilarious to be in a tight spot, fighting cannibals, and you turn over the card you really need and it's... "Moronic", as in you're so nuts from living alone on an island that you've lost your marbles.

Great for playing with kids, if you act as a team.

Addictive!

RATING: 7.5
This one is a strange duck, at least for me - a solo game with Euro mechanisms that works!  Likely this is the case because it was designed as a solo game only.  Most Euros with a solo option (like almost all of Rosenberg's offerings) are distinctly uninspiring, in that you are basically puzzling your way to a high score.  With Friday, you are trying to kill pirates, not score better than last time, so the theme is there, and happily the game is decently tough, even in "normal" mode.  Is this the only FF I have left in my collection?  How did that happen?  (Don't answer that).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Very challenging game with some really clever, thematic mechanics. It's a brilliant touch to have the aging cards get introduced to your deck every time you deplete it, keeping you from culling too many of your weaker cards. On the other hand, you absolutely need to get rid of some cards to make your deck more efficient. Finding the right balance between them is key.

Unfortunately I have not yet been able to find that balance. I frankly don't believe people who say they won their first game (or who win most of the games they play), but I'm also notoriously bad at deck builders, so what do I know? I've played 6 times now and still haven't won. The good thing is that this means I have lots of challenging playtime ahead of me.

RATING: 8
Played a couple times (both losses), and it's pretty clever and fun. And not easy - food is very tight. You can't be cavalier about spending food to win challenges. It seems to be all about identifying cards you need to add to your deck, knowing when to take risks to try to get the really good cards, and what to do when you have a lost challenge but not enough good cards to destroy. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Deckbuilding fans: you owe it to yourselves to check out Friday, whether solo gaming is usually your thing or not. I'm not generally a solo gamer, but Friday caught my eye awhile back and I'm very glad I tried it! 

There's a lot to like about what Friday brings to the deckbuilding formula. The main source of tension is in the hazard cards - every turn you must encounter one and fight against it. Here's the catch, though: winning AND losing fights are equally important. You have to decide which fights to win and which you're better off losing - and you can lose a fair amount of health doing either. Wins net you new, more powerful cards for your deck while losses allow you to trash unwanted cards from your deck.

It gives the game a nice choice point during turns (something not all deckbuilders have) and trying to win a fight often involves a small press-your-luck element as you pay life to draw new cards and rely on your knowledge of what's left in the deck and lady luck to bring you a win.

Another welcome little wrinkle in the design comes from the aging cards - essentially, every time you cycle your deck you must add in a penalty card. It's a really clever way to discourage pruning your deck too much and adds just that extra little bit of friction to make things interesting.

Mechanically this game is probably more like an 8, but I personally don't find upping difficulty levels in these sorts of games to be all that thrilling so now that I've conquered it on one difficulty level I can't see it getting super frequent play.

High Score: Level 1 - 68

RATING: 5

I think for me the two main downsides are that three times through the fight deck feels like one too many times and the fact that managing the different decks throughout the game felt tedious. If this was an app I'd probably have a lot of fun with it, but at this point I'd rather get out the Star Realms app or something from the Oniverse and play through that.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Great little solitaire game with the neat conceit that obstacles beaten with your deck turn into new cards, while older and worse cards can be removed by losing to those same obstacles.  Unless your deck is well-tuned, you will progressively lose life points with either option, so the game becomes an interesting mix of balancing adding new cards, destroying old ones, and managing your supply of life points such that you are making progress while still being insulated from disaster.  Add 'aging' into this, which serves as a timer by adding a bad card every time you cycle through your deck, and there's a nice range of decisions to make in every game.  Randomization keeps it spiced up, as is usually the case in solitaires; you know the initial configuration of your deck, but the hazards/opportunities, aging cards, and the pirates you fight at the end change every game. I can see somewhere around 50-100 plays coming out of this before it gets old.

Production values are good, with humorous art, nice life tokens repurposed from Furstenfeld, and some probably extraneous play mats in a little square box.  Setup takes a little while, maybe five minutes out of the box, but resets of the game once you lose (or win maybe) are a little shorter.  It takes up a bit of space on the table, so probably not an airplane game, though the ingenious traveler could probably manage by ditching the mats and using a different system to track life points.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Great little solitaire game.

RATING: 8
Vendu Kev*
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.25
There's something inherently sad about playing a board game by yourself, so purchasing a game that can ONLY be played solo makes for a rather depressing transaction.  But undeniably, this is a niche that needed filling for me and many others, and Friday fills it with aplomb.  

The way the game progresses and forms a sort of narrative arc is really clever; you always feel completely unprepared and under-powered, and most of your victories feel like they're by the skin of your teeth.  Yet somehow, by the time you reach the seemingly impossible pirates, you have quite a lot of tactical options, and can sometimes just steamroll right over them.

Negatives are that it can become a bit difficult to keep track of what abilities you have and haven't used in some of the bigger fights.  

Also, I could be wrong,  but with the way the aging deck is implemented, it seems unwise to ever go after the harder hazards if you can avoid them; the big rewards aren't better enough than the small ones to justify going through your Robinson Deck so much faster.  So the game might suffer from lack of strategic variety, or perhaps I'm the one lacking the imagination to see other viable paths to victory.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
In this solo adventure, you're doing a little deck-building, continually trying to burn bad cards while overcoming hazards to add in some good cards.  If you haven't drawn enough good cards to defeat a hazard, you can give up precious life points to draw more.

Most cards have a special ability which is where the real meat of the game takes place.  All the while you're balancing two decks which accelerate the game each time you shuffle, leading you towards a very tough confrontation with some pirates.

I want to love this, but so far I just like it.  I can see playing this regularly until securing a win - but will the increased difficulty levels be enough to sustain interest in the long-term?  I'm not sure.

RATING: 9
Very fun and interesting little deck building game. Much more deeper than seems at first. Although the game variance seems not to be very strong (the winning strategy is quite similar in each game), the tactic decisions are interesting each game.
So far one of the best options for me when I want to play some quick solo game. Also this is my choice when I plan to play outside my house - it is very portable and the game itself is very relaxing and easygoing.

What I like:
- I like the deckbuilding part of the game, for the mostly trash like deck you built a powerful one. And every mistake you did during the process will come back for you.
- The game is very portable, just a pack of cards and some tokens. You even don't need the little boards to play it.
- Game time is perfect for me. Although It is not short as for example in The Lost Expedition or Mint Works, the average time is cca 20-25 minutes for me and I always want to play one more game.
- After 100 games I am still not tired of it at all. Contrary, as I know the game more, I believe I enjoy it even more.

What I dislike:
- final fights could be tougher, you should win almost everytime when you get there.
- the art is somewhat cartoonish and not very well put (compare with once mentioned The Lost Legion). The card images are samey with just some different detail. But I must say that I don't look at card images during play in general so this is only a minor issue.
- Sleeves. There is no good sleeves available for this game. And You will need them - there is a lot of shuffling. I have sleeved it, but the sleeves are a bit bigger and very soft. I can imagine how it should be played with proper premium sleeves

RATING: 8
Very clever deck management game. The balance and decisions between adding more cards to the fighting deck vs thinning out the cruddy cards (at the cost of life points) is very subtle and entertaining. And that's when you've already got past the basic decisions of going for easy or hard hazards. And the fact this also feeds into how fast you churn the fighting deck (and hence age Robinson) makes for some tricky choices.
Plays very well and fast. Definitely one of the better 1 player games out there. An absolute bargain at the asking price.

(Hard to rate it an 8, since who would "I suggest it" to given its a solo game? But its an 8 anyway.)

RATING: 6
[2012-03-12 Rating: n.a. -> 6]
Friday is a nice solo deck builder. I like it's puzzle aspect, I enjoyed all my plays of it and it surely has some replayability. So why no higher rating? In the end, I wish this would be an electronic game. For a solo game, it surely needs a lot of table space and forces you to do a lot of (simple) math in your head, especially in the last few rounds. Maybe, this could have been a little more streamlined.

Also, I wish they had used square cards instead of the rectangle ones that are included in the box. Since you have to rotate them after they have been used, you mess with your layout all the time.

All in all, I would recommend Friday to gamers who like solo games. For the prize it is sold, you can't do anything wrong.

RATING: 4
This game is just so-so. I knew going into it that the theme wouldn't (and still doesn't) appeal to me. I typically like solo card games, but this one just missed for me. I can't quite put my finger on why, but every single turn just felt dry and uninteresting. Perhaps it had to do with the way you defeat a challenge: drawing X cards and checking if you number is bigger than the challenge's. The special abilities of the cards added some mild variety to the turn, but none of the cards combined in truly interesting ways and the whole deck-building aspect felt lackluster. The aging cards also felt a bit weird to me, as thinning your deck is supposed to be a core tenant of deck-builders. However, Friday punishes you every time you cycle through your deck, making deck thinning an much less attractive (and viable) tactic.

Maybe I'll come back to this one later and it will surprise me, but quite frankly I'd rather spend my time playing any one of the Oniverse games instead.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
A solitaire game where the player is Man Friday, training Robinson Crusoe for his battle against the pirates.  A nice little deck churning card game.  The player flips up two "encounter" cards and chooses one to tackle.  Cards are then flipped from the "Crusoe" deck to either defeat the encounter, or be defeated.  If the encounter is defeated, you get the card to add to your deck - typically a good thing.  If you are defeated, it drains your life, but you get to trim your deck and get rid of weaker cards - making you stronger (deck) and weaker (life) at the same time.  After three runs through the "encounter" deck, hopefully your Crusoe deck and life is solid enough to defeat the pirates.  Fantastic solitaire game - mechanically simple, but serves up some tough choices for the player.  A gem.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Friday is a fun "solo adventure" that uses deck-building as it's central mechanism. The game has a nice arc to it, as you help Robinson navigate the green, yellow, and red phases, and then the final showdown with two pirates. 

During each phase, there are winning strategies to develop your fight deck engine. The final showdown is fun, because many fight cards will be drawn as you use the cards special abilities (+1/2 cards, exchange, copy).

Friday does play similarly each time. Once you understand the winning strategy, you just need to execute it. The final showdown pirates do not offer much variability: the strategy against them all is to build that fight deck engine and then let it run. I wish that the different pirates would force the player to tune the fight deck a certain way (but they don't).

I think it curious that many commenters consider this game to be "hard". After several learning plays, I now rarely lose (on Level 4). Perhaps because I have played all the Oniverse games, I have sufficient experience with randomness mitigation strategies that are common to solitaire games. I do consider all of the Oniverse games to be deeper experiences with juicier decisions.

I'm happy I bought, learned, and now own and play Friday. It's a small game and rather inexpensive, and I've definitely got my money's worth.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
The beginning of the Great Solo Initiative of 2017. For years I had a strong affinity for cooperative games because my wife liked them so much.  I got a LOT of coops so my wife would play with me.... In the fall of 2016 (six weeks after my stroke) my wife left me. By early 2017 it was clear she had no intention of coming back any time soon. Now coops leave me feeling a little empty. So begins my quest for solo games. The first one I bought in this flurry was Friday .... and boy does Friday set the bar high!

At its heart it's a mini deck builder. You'really helping "Robinson" (the rules make it clear that the character is "based on" Robinson Crusoe) prepare to battle pirates at the end of the game. You do this by facing wild animals (which apparently include chickens, based on artwork on the cards) cannibals, and exploring the island. These events give Robinson weapons and experience, but through the whole game Robinson also ages, slowing him down and limiting his fighting abilities. 

This game is smart and tight. But most of all it is fun. It's a 45 minute game that I play back-to-back-to-back. This will be the solo standard for years.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9

The mechanics are easy as you draw and either defeat the obstacle or spend life points to draw more cards/get rid of cards.  It gets more and more difficult as you go on and that is definitely a good thing as you will be wracking your brain to do certain moves while avoiding aging cards that hinder your progress.

RATING: 6
(Revised from 9)
Am I playing this wrong? As the losses have stacked up, my interest in this game has cooled off considerably. I've tried multiple strategies, and read all the forums, and I still suck at this game. I want to have fun, not get kicked in the face over and over and over...

(Old review) 

So basically, I should never end up on a deserted island, because I'd be dead in like 5 minutes, if Friday is anything to go by. 

The learning curve, thus far, is fairly steep on this game. Perhaps it is akin to climbing a mountain, in that you must take it one battle at a time. The battles that I have fought hard, and won, using special skills, and pushing my luck, have been quite satisfying. When death comes, and the game ends, I feel resigned, and thoughtful. "What would I do different next time?" "What worked well?" "What definitely didn't work, at all?"

Decent card stock, clever design/mechanics; an elegant, fun little game, with some big moments.

RATING: 7
First game in a long time that I've played solo more than once.  The design is really quite brilliant, with lots of interesting decisions and risk management.

Do you pay life to draw extra cards and beat the encounter?  Or do you pay life to escape instead so you can cull the crap out of your deck.  Make your deck too small and you'll age too quickly.  Do you risk going after the big encounters while they're still relatively weak, or pick the easy encounters and conserve cards?

Best thing about it -- no having to beg somebody else to play a game with you!

RATING: 8.5
Wow.  What an amazing solitaire game!  So much fun to play.  It's very challenging, and you have to use your cards just right to have good chance at winning.

Once the player reaches the pirates, the game game goes from very good to "epic".  Don't be surprised if you need to cycle through your Robinson deck a few times... drawing card after card... reshuffling and drawing card after card again (and spending LIFE to do so).  It's at these moments that yield "nail-biting" suspense and you need to carefully contemplate ALL strategic options for one false move and you will lose!  It's a great game to have in your collection, and I don't see myself tiring of it anytime soon.  Grade: B+/A-

RATING: 8
The best pure solo/solitaire board game you can get right now. The game offers varying amount of difficulty and is quite challenging. You make your deck stronger by removing weak cards and gaining stronger ones that make defeating encounters easier. You will have a harder time acquiring cards as you will have many cards that do not add anything to your attack value or worse has a minus value. After going through the final hazard level you will have to defeat the 2 pirates that you draw from the start of the game. The game is very easy to learn and understand and the most challenging thing to understand about the game is the interaction of the card text effects and how they work. The instruction book makes it very clear how it can be used and there is good video on youtube that explains all the game effects very well. Very small game size which makes it another great stocking stuffer and portable game. I highly recommend this game if you are looking for a great solo game!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Purchased as handy solo game.  Do remember that you start off with 5 plus points over 4 cards and 5 minus points over 5 cards in the deck, as well as the 9 zeros, so if you choose a hazard card with a 4 or 5 before you have won any additional fighting cards you are going to lose against it and have to pay heavily - only worthwhile to get rid of minus cards if you have a run.  Having not picked it off the shelf for a year or two it took me a game to get back into, but really the rules are fairly straightforward once your brain is in gear.  Choose your hazard card.  Fight it with your free card draw allowance.  If you haven't beaten or equalled the hazard value, which enables you to add the hazard to your fighting card deck,  choose to pay a life per card to continue fighting it with additional cards, or pay the hazard value in played cards plus lives for the card to go away till the next round, discarding as many of your undesirable fighting cards as possible up to the number of lives you have paid to get rid of it.  Special abilities enable you to add or lose lives, draw or destroy cards for free, reduce the hazard value, copy abilities of already played cards etc.  If you survive three rounds of hazards then you can try to beat two pirate cards which have high values and often special conditions.  Plenty of replay value for occasional players, but not enough strategy for me to be interested in regular play. Might feel differently if I were on a desert island.......

RATING: 8
What a weird and wonderful little game.  You actually feel like you're training and getting stronger as the game progresses.

Second play: Wow.  Even more clever than I originally thought.  There are a lot more meaningful decisions to be made than I first thought.  Minor quibble: there are a lot of opportunities to miss small rules or miscount.  My second play was a lot smoother than the first though and I found myself referring to the rulebook only a few times.

Broke this out on a whim...so interesting.  Is there an optimal strategy?  Obviously, trashing bad cards is very important, but having to choose between the two hazards that come up each turn takes some thinking.  Do I go for the higher point value knowing that if I fail, I can trash cards?  Do I pick the easier one to save life points, knowing it may hurt me in the long run?  Do I pick the card purely for the special ability?  0-3 so far.  I need to play this several times in a row tonight.

Sweet mother of god, my first victory with 26 points.  Not a great score, but I'm just happy I finally won.  

Argh - instead of thinning the deck, I thought I'd see what would happen if I tried conquering as many hazards as possible and just use the Destroy special ability cards to drop the weak initial cards.  I couldn't defeat the second pirate card (40 HP).

After 8 plays, as a solitaire game, this one is pretty hard to beat.  It plays in under 20 minutes, and set-up is fast.  I'm starting to have concerns about it getting played out eventually, but since I'm still playing at the introductory difficulty level, I can't be sure yet.  

Moved on to Level 4.  Lost my first game before even meeting the pirates.  

Yet to win on Level 4.  It's a tough one, and just getting to the red stage is a feat in itself.

Level 1 record: 3-5  
Level 1 high score: 97 points

Level 4 record: 0-12
Level 4 high score:

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Friday is a well-crafted solitaire game with some subtlety. The game works so well because it presents you with multiple goals that are often incompatible.

Your deck starts off being absolutely terrible. Most of the cards have zero or negative values. In order to get rid of those cards, you actually need to lose fights. Losing fights drains your life points and brings you closer to death, but it also allows you to learn from the experience and trash one or more of the cards you played that turn. But in order to get better cards into your deck, you need to win fights. Just knowing whether you're trying to win or lose a fight is not always easy.

Another tension involves the deck cycling. On one hand, you want to cycle your deck quickly because you are constantly improving it. On the other hand, you must add an "aging" card to your deck every time it runs out - and these are terrible, nasty cards.

Mentally keeping track of what's left in your deck is very important. Be smart about which challenges to face early. You'll want to cycle your deck quickly so that you have as much power as possible by the time you reach the yellow challenges. This means tackling many of the harder challenges right from the very start, just to cycle your deck and pay to dispose of most of your bad cards.

Friday does an outstanding job of conveying its plot and setting, which is especially impressive for a small, mechanically-slick card game like this. At the start of the game, our "hero" Robinson Crusoe is a bumbling fool who doesn't have the skills and knowledge to survive in the wild. As he decides what risks he is willing to take, you can guide him in learning new skills and eliminating the worst of his mistakes. By the end of the game, he is haggard and worn, but also cunning and deadly. Where the balance lies will determine whether you survive the expedition.

Journal of Friday's Expeditions:

Level 1: dead, 115

Level 2: 54, 159

Level 3: (skipped)

Level 4: dead, 63, 82, 113, dead, dead, 78

RATING: 7
Surprisingly challenging solo deckbuilder.  Definitely a right way and a wrong way to play this game and win it.  I've beat it on the hardest level, but you need some luck, and don't make any mistakes.  One of the best solo games I've ever played.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
There's a lot of big decisions and lots of game in this little box. Every turn there is an event and first you have to choose whether you want to challenge or lose. Losing allows you to remove cards from your deck but it also removes life points. If you decide to challenge there is still a chance that you'll lose but if you win you get to keep the event card. This way you will strengthen your deck. You don't want your deck too bloated because there aren't that many powerful cards to keep and you don't want your deck too thin because every time you have no more cards to draw you have to add an aging card to your deck which are the worst cards in the game and cost 2 life to remove.

Pros:

-Antoine de Saint-Exupery said "Perfection is achieved not when there is nothing more to add, but when there is nothing left to take away" and I think he'd be delighted after playing this game. All the fat has been trimmed and only the absolutely essential gears that cause this game to run have been left behind. This might be the most streamlined game I have ever enjoyed playing. Nothing feels like it has been sacrificed to fit in the box or to meet a certain playing time. It's damn near a perfect design.

-It's portable. All you need are the cards really. The lifepoints can be tracked on paper or you can use coins or M&Ms.

-Don't let the simplicity of the game fool you, this game is hard to beat. I'm more than a dozen games in and I don't have a near fool proof strategy yet. The one time I did win might have had more to do with luck and intuition than it did clinical decision making.

-Almost each card has a special effect which allows you to set up cool combinations when those cards get drawn. Also there are different Pirate abilities so there's a nice selection of end game bosses that will change your strategy according to what you'll be up against.

-I like games with a level system or a timer. In Friday there are three levels of difficulty that you will be advancing throughout the game and this gives me a good guideline to what kind of fight points I should be pulling out of my deck, which makes it easier for me to gauge where I should be.



Cons:

-I don't know why the cards have to be such a weird shape. I thought about sleeving this game but then I looked for sleeves and they don't even make a sleeve this size. What the Hell Friese?

-There isn't a lot of depth here and I'm a guy who likes depth. After you run through the game once there aren't really any rulebook checking or going down different roads to victory in the game and this stuff I love.


All in all Friday is a fantastic little game. It's portable, it's cheap and there is plenty of replayability here.

8/10

RATING: 7
Very enjoyable solo game with rich decision making -- do you whiff fights to 'learn from them' (i.e.,trim your deck at the expense of receiving crippling aging cards as you cycle through your deck faster), pick challenges you might not stand up to so easily (but will leave you in a terrific position moving forward), take the easy route and hope the pirates you face at the end of the game don't grind you into the ground? All in all, Friday does a really great job of capturing the desert island survival theme and provides interesting decisions (and enough luck and variability so that the game is never solvable) to make for a solid and quick solo game.

RATING: 7.25
Friday is a challenging little deck-builder, with aspects of Thunderstone style themed deck-building, tuned to a solo gaming focus and with a decent dash of Pandemic style deck-driven events.

Players need to thin their decks by losing to island perils, but they also need to accumulate more useful action cards by defeating the island perils, while maintaining a good stock of life tokens and also clearing out the barrier aging cards.

All of this requires some difficult decision making, and a little luck of the decks involved.

The artwork is simple, but appropriate, the price-point is low, and the gameplay is... well, let's just say I haven't won the game yet, or worn it out.

I like this game, but I don't love it- on the other hand I think it does what it sets out to accomplish quite well.

After about 4 games I think this starts at a 6.75 for me.  We'll see whether it grows on me more over time or not.

PS: Noticed a major rules miss on my part, enabling Friday to spend additional lives for more fighting cards, and won for the 1st time on my 8th game.

This greatly enhanced the interest for me- it made it possible to win!- and that change makes this an easy 7.25 rank.

RATING: 7.5
This, and my game (LOTR: the adventure deck game) are the only games (both short card games) that I love to play again, again, and again, anytime I can.
I usually play 4-5 games a day of Friday... And I payed 15 euros for it: I certainly got my money's worth.

The game is a lot deeper than one may think at first and lends to lots of decisions, both tactic-wise and strategy-wise. My favorite decisions are when I realize, throughout the game, that I need to thicken my deck, or destro a few aging cards, or that my deck is too slim, and I run into too many aging cards.
The results are visible right away, and it's a lovely feeling, that you get rewarded for planning, and thinking.

Great game.
Dunno how long I'm going to play it, as I think I wore it out, but, it's a great great game.

EDIT: Dropped from 9 to 7: after many (MANY) plays, the game became beatable in SO many ways, I can't play it anymore. I might play it again but I get no more challenge from it. It's a keeper though, as it still is a GREAT game.

RATING: 7
Its a very nice theme, fairly portable, fairly fast and very easy to learn, rules were quite clear mostly and in the end I think its a well designed game, more so than most of the FF titles I have played, this could be his 2nd best!  

The theme comes through a little, but not as much as I hoped without mechanics really supporting it, what you have here is almost a pure deckbuilder. I have not played many other solo type games so don't have much to compare to, but it seems to me things were well thought out here and/or playtested well from what I can tell so far. 

There are some decisions to make here, more so than Onirim for a comparison anyway. You have to decide how fast to trim down your deck, and then how fast to add back to it as well, those are your main over-arching decisions, then there are smaller micro ones that which cards to toast and which to add, how many life points you should spend and when and where to push your luck. So far, these decisions feel meaningful to me, where as in Onirim they did not largely due to luck being too big of factor, its a factor here too of course but much less so far as I can tell for now anyway.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This game is very clever. I am not a huge fan of deck building games but it works extremely well here. You start with a deck of fighting cards with combat values or -1, 0, 1, and 2. The average strength is zero. Each turn you draw two hazard cards and choose one to battle. Hazard cards have a value you need to equal or exceed with fighting cards, and a number of fighting cards you're allowed to draw for free. You can draw more at the cost of 1 life point each. If you fail to beat the hazard you have the chance to remove some of the fighting cards used from the game. If you win you get the hazard card which has a fighting card printed on it's lower half. 

There are lots of interesting decisions here. Do I want to win the battle or loose to get rid of cards. If I do want to win what are the odds given the current make up of my deck. Am I willing to spend life points to push for victory? 

You go through the hazard deck three times, with the threats increasing in difficulty each pass. Then you must fight two pirate cards which are essentially very challenging hazards. 

The theme is surprisingly well integrated. Each time you go through your deck you age and add an ageing card (sight unseen) to your deck. Ageing cards are bad, but you can get rid of them at a cost.

The game is tough and has a scaling difficulty, giving a good amount of replay value. You calculate a score at the end, but you only win if you can defeat the pirates. I prefer solo games that have a definitive pass/fail ending since this makes for exciting game play, much more so than calculating a number and comparing it to past games. Of course those numbers are interesting too so it seems Friedemann Friese wants to have it both ways here, and I think it works well.

I have only played a handful of times so far, but I am a bit concerned that I will fall into the same style of play every game. I'm not sure how the different pirates will really influence my deck construction. It seems I always want the best cards regardless of which pirates are in play.

A tedious game, if indeed it is a game. The theme is tissue-paper thin, and I was underwhelmed by the mechanics. RATING: 7
Players: 1
Time: 25 minutes
Inspired by Robinson Crusoe, you deal with hazards in three increasingly difficult phases. Over time, you can cull bad cards and gain better cards as you prepare to battle two different groups of pirates (different each game). Essentially, this game forces you to manage your health, as it is needed to draw extra cards and is spent when you lose against a hazard. This is a quick and enjoyable solo game.

RATING: 9
Disclaimer: I played 3 times and lost every time. 

Game is hard to win, but very addictive: once you "get it", there is that One More Play feeling. There are enough choices at each turn, theme feels good. At first it may seem there is not much variation in the cards but there is plenty in the combination of the cards.

Manual:  the manual does not take you by the hand. It consists of two leaflets. One shows the setup, the other describes the game round. It is important to sort the cards on the amount of green "hearts" in the corner first, and keep the special -3 very stupid out. The manual does not mention that. I had to re-read the manuals several times, and after watching some yt reviews I finally got it right.

A minus point for the bad manual and the fact that even on easy the game will be too hard for the majority of gamers (let alone the human population).

The game has 22 wooden chits that don't even resemble hearts, but the 2 are never used so what's the use? I can't see how anyone can say this game is repetitive - the pirate ships are very different each time and sensational. 

I bought the dutch version for 10 euro from summoner, sealed and new and all.

RATING: 6
Awesome solo deck builder with various levels of difficultly.  I lost in my first play, but that only makes me want to beat this game even more.  I really like how the life tokens are manipulated for losing against hazard cards or for simply for drawing additional Robinson cards.  The ability to thin cards from your deck after a loss is genius.  The three step levels help prepare your deck against the final pirate attack.  Every time though your deck you have to add an aging card.  Everything works beautifully.

RATING: 8.5
Brilliantly designed mechanics and solid gameplay. Friese brings the same important decisions and focus on calculation to this game as to other titles. The game features a 'normal mode' and a 'hard mode', but apart from these, each game is very much like the others (the random pirates don't seem to make much difference to me, but perhaps it's more obvious on hard mode).

An excellent solo that's worth playing (and playing until you win) at least once. I think the replay value is too low to make it a permanent part of my collection.

RATING: 7
nice solo game.  I usually don't record solo plays of games but as this is solo only, I will.  Reminds me a lot of Pathfinder Adventure Card Game solo.  Both involve weighing sacrificing life against building your deck.  While PAC may be a more interesting game because of the adventure path and persistent characters, I think this offers more interesting tactical decisions.  They play in about the same time.  can I justify owning both?  Friday is much easier to set up.

Also a winner thematically.  I really like how it models how Crusoe overcomes obstacles or deals with failure.  And the aging process.  Really well done.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I thought I was good at deck builders. I was wrong. After 6 attempts at the easiest level, I still haven't been able to encounter the pirate ships. This is probably a really good thing though, because once you learn how to beat the game, I feel like each game experience would feel way too similar. 

I really like though how you want to lose hazards sometimes, and ideally by a specific amount in order to cull your bad cards. Also the choices of which hazard to encounter and ability to manipulate what you draw next makes this game have decisions besides deciding what you want to go after and sticking with it as a lot of deck builders have an issue with, although the number of deadweight cards in this game make it hard to get combos going and makes it lose that engine building feel.

Not a fan of the artwork, and when playing quickly since there is very minimal artwork differences it can be easy to miss ability differences between cards.

RATING: 7
I only got this recently, but it is awesome. I wouldn't compare it to solitaire. You are playing cards from different decks against each other, and rather than building straights from alternating red/black as in Solitaire, there's a whole story going on in Friday, with hazards and events galore.
Great box, great (amusing) cards, neat lifepoints that aren't just generic eurogame pieces, great gameplay, simple rules with a lot of depth and replayability... it's got a lot in a little box.
Couldn't ask for more. Not only the least expensive but also the most fun solo-only game I own (solo-only meaning it is made for 1 player, and no official rules for 2+P exist).

RATING: 9
Man, this is a good little game! Small box, relatively few components (and the boards aren't even strictly necessary -- this should travel really well), but lots to think about. Even on a first play it comes in pretty close to its listed play time; it's short but very sweet.

Friday started hitting my radar around the time I began getting tired of deckbuilding, so I initially dismissed it. I'm glad I changed my mind and gave it a shot, because the deckbuilding is incredibly well implemented, not an afterthought in any way, and a lot of fun.

The whole game is fun, in fact. The artwork is charming, the theme is cute, and it's a challenging game even at level 1. It has a puzzle-like quality that I enjoy, and I can see that it's going to be enjoyable to try and conquer it at higher difficulties.

---

Five plays, two wins, and Friday moves from an 8 to a 9. This is a gem, particularly because it can be played so quickly yet delivers a satisfying and challenging experience within its short play time. After a few games I rarely need the rulebook, too.

RATING: 7
After 8 plays:

Feel like I have the rules and basic strategy down (at least for lvl 1).

A deck building game that essentially involves sacrificing life to toss bad initial cards, while building in more powerful cards (careful consideration needs to be given to when to push for these).  

I quite like how the mechanic ties in with the theme - Robinson's experiences make him stronger in two ways: 1) causing him to lose his weaker traits when he evades a tough encounter, and 2) gaining new strengths when he overcomes encounters.

Plays quickly, very portable.  All up, a nice little game.

After over 30 plays, I still haven't mastered this game. Each game really does play out differently, although my life points are always very tight, it seems. The Phase -1 card is a must to do well, win it at all costs!

The battles against the pirates can be a little tedious. It's fun to combine all the different abilities earned throughout the game, but I'll need to figure out a sensible way of keeping track of just how many fighting points are on the table when there are 15-20 cards in play.

RATING: 8
It's a format solitaire gamers know, but the changes made to the typical structure work so well that it will surely lead to many a forehead slap and an exclamation along the lines of, "why has no one done this before?"  By cards having dual purposes, allowing dangers to be selected, not including specific "this trumps this card, unless trumped by this card" situation, and working through the deck multiple times it completely eliminates the basic issue of entirely being at the mercy of the deck, or in the most basic terms, minimizes the role of luck.  I think it easy to say it established a new standard for this type of solo game

RATING: 5
I do find this game to have some interesting challenges and decisions, but I don't think I'll play it too often. If I want to play a boardgame on my own I'm spoilt by a great choice of fantastic iPad versions of games.

This game feels a bit like work, a sort of fine line between a brain-teasing challenge and tedium. The gradual deck-building can feel repetitive. Actually managing all the cards and decks isn't to bad; the game runs smoothly and there is very little set-up (there is lots of shuffling during the game, however).

If I feel in the mood for an 'analog' solitaire experience it'll be by far my first choice. I might just be more inclined to read a good book, that's all.

RATING: 7
[microbadge=1714]

[u]16-Jan-2013[/u]: Hmmm...what can I say about this [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/blog/1597/mo-plays-friday-100-times]that I haven't already said[/url]?  I love this game.  It's portable.  It's easy on your wallet.  It's fun.  It's challenging.  This is an all around fantastic solitaire game.

Admittedly, this eventually comes down to a game of numbers.  Will your deck be strong enough to beat the ever increasing strength of the hazards you will face along the way?  I think the theme is there if want it to be.  And it is a fun one.  The artwork, while a little cartoony, really does add to the flavor of the game.

If you enjoy deck building games like Dominion and are looking for some solitaire time, this is definitely your game.

[u]24-Jan-2014[/u]:  Yep...still [b][i]rocks![/i][/b]

RATING: 8.5
A deckbuilder. Wait, keep reading!

You start out with a fighting deck (same deck every time, only shuffled) that kinda sucks. You flip over two hazards and choose one to fight. Do I fight the easier one with my crap deck and get the bonus the hazard provides, or do I lose to the harder one but get to kill the crap cards in my starting deck that I flipped over? If I discard the harder one, I'll have to fight it again after reshuffling the hazard deck, only instead of fighting it on green level, I'll have to fight it on yellow level. But my deck will be much better by that point. Of course, each time you reshuffle your fighting deck, you add in an aging card which can absolutely screw you over at a crucial moment no matter how good your hand is. And say you're fighting a higher-end hazard with your great deck and pull out that aging card. Balls. It doesn't lose the game for me but it might in the next runthrough of the fighting deck. But I really wanted to win this hazard I'm fighting because it provides a +2 life special ability and I'm so close to beating it! So do I lose now so I can kill the aging card (knowing full well that I'll never be able to beat the hazard the next time it comes around on red level)? Or do I eat it and win? There is so much uncertainty and risk management, and it's all so simply laid out! Wonderful game.

*edit* After playing this more and more, I love it. I love pulling it out. I love playing it. It's really grown on me and I can't see it stopping until I master it on the hardest level. I also have played Thunderstone Advance and Mage Knight: Boardgame. While the others have their pros, this game has them beat in terms of the ultimate deckbuilding mechanic. It's perfection! Ok, close to perfection. It's a 9. The only reason I give it 1 mark off is because this is not a game I'll be playing forever. I'll eventually master it and never touch it again. Having said that, attempting to master it is enjoyably addictive!

*update* Having played many other games, this game is still awesome. But I'm lowering it to an 8.5
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10
I really love this game.  It's a character-builder/deck-builder game, and it changes every time you play it.  You are playing against the game - just like traditional solitaire - so don't expect to win very often.  But the ebb and flow of the game is really solid - with the character of Robinson beginning as a dummy without many skills, and gaining skills as you beat challenges.  But beware, take too long to beat challenges, and Robinson ages - causing him to take minuses!  It's really tricky to play to gain good cards while also removing bad cards.  Strategy is key!

This is a really good solitaire puzzle.

-> zero interaction (duh!)
-> I need a mental break!
-> like card solitaires, I need variety after a while
+ its' best attributes are its' worst faults!  short, simple, solo, challenging

While I cannot rate it a 10 for BGG, I highly recommend this for solo play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
It is a solitaire game that doesn't introduce any revolutionary concept. It's just a deck building game with a push your luck element added onto it, and some other twists. For example, you will spend life points to filter your deck, and once you exhaust it you will add aging cards that will penalize you; if you filter it too thin, aging cards will kill you.

It's a matter of finding a balance bewteen these concepts and some others, and forming a deck able to defeat the always difficult final enemies.

Once you figure out the balance needed to beat the game, it's a matter the draw of the luck. There are several final enemies, but they are too similar. And as I said, solo games are not my cup of tea. That means its replay value is quite low for me.

The manual has some holes, some things are not well explained. The cards are OK, they have an odd size that fits their content. The mats are not necessary and the life points wooden tokens are wheat spikes... Why?

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.25
心得:
蠻不錯的單人算牌遊戲
主要策略應該是在第一輪用完自己牌庫時
盡量把0跟-1的牌清掉
phase-1的牌不一定要有
+2牌跟+1或是+生命牌都蠻強的
第二輪自己的牌盡量要想辦法拿sort或exchange還有destroy
後期看情況可能也要清掉些低攻擊力的牌
另外策略點是不一定要抽到免費抽得牌數，要看狀況停止
規則:
1.起始將老化牌分強度洗勻，最強的三張放下面，剩下七張放上面(-3拿掉)
2.隨機抽兩張海盜牌，難度牌黃綠紅疊在一起
3.個人牌堆，探索牌推各自洗勻，照難度拿生命
4.每回盒抽兩張探險卡，則一探險根據目前難度得數字，跟該探險卡可抽的免費卡抽牌，抽牌一張一張抽，免費牌數可不抽滿，免費牌放左邊
5.可用1生命抽一張牌，牌放在探險牌右邊
6.牌的功能使用完後橫置
7.功能結束後，成功把所有剩下牌根探險牌丟進棄牌推，失敗，數值差多少掉多少命，且可移牌出遊戲
8.剩一張探險牌時可選擇挑戰或不挑戰，結束後難度提升一級，紅色難度完就挑戰海盜
9.每次牌庫不夠抽就加一張蓋著的年老卡並洗牌
10.贏兩個海盜，或是生命低於0(可等於)，或是全卡用完打不贏海盜皆結束遊戲
11.抽牌能力放在右邊，每張雙倍只能作用在一張卡，排序三張可看下三張任意排序，且可棄一張，交換棄一張抽一張，交換兩張如果要用第一張來換第二張，第一張能力不可用，放在牌庫底如果是拿免費牌，可補抽一張
12.四個難度 A: 20命 B: 隨機加一張年老卡 C: -3年老卡洗入年老牌堆 D: 18命
13.記分:所有牌數值相加，年老卡總是-5 + 15分一張海盜卡 + 5分每命 -3分每張沒完成的探險卡

RATING: 7
荒島求生記
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A deck builder that's so finely tuned that every decision you make, and you make one every turn, seems vital. You start with a deck of mostly bad cards. Each turn you flip two encounters and choose one of them to "battle" (ie flip x cards and you need y points on your flipped cards to win). Win, and the card you just bought gets added to your deck - it'll be better than the cards you have plus it'll have a cool power (like draw more cards, double another card's points, etc). Lose, and you lose life points (you only have so many) but as compensation you get to thin your deck and remove low value cards (which you also need to do). But you don't get the cool new card. And you're only allowed to thin if you have enough life points left to spend. Lose all of them and you've lost. So sometimes you aim to lose, sometimes to win, and knowing which when seems the key to the game. To win, you need to get through the encounter deck three times (and each time the score needed to win gets higher) and then beat two big boss pirate encounters. And each time you go through your deck, a bad card gets added, so you may not want to thin your deck too much, or take too many cards with powers to draw more cards. Finding the right balance given how the cards come out (and there's obviously a bunch of luck in that) is the charm of the game. It adds replay by having 4 levels of difficulty to work your way up, each level seemingly a small step, but it's surprising how big a difference that small step makes. It's good value if you enjoy patience type solo games.

RATING: 10
I got to thinking “this is a 10” after about 6 to 8 plays. It took time to appreciate the genius design of this game. It takes some plays to understand rules and card instructions and nuances. When you do everything clicks and each game is quick and full of hurrahs or aws. It’s smooth how you as Friday help Robinson get over his weaknesses and guide him to gain experience. As that goes on aging takes place but when guided well it is countered by the use of tools, expertise, and better weapons. If all is chosen well you lead Robinson to dominate the island. This grueling exercise in turn prepares him for the final battles against the pirates. In my case for every time i felt that something was too hard or too easy or that it didn’t make good sense I stopped and took another look at the rules and at the posts on bgg. This answered all questions that I had and the next two or three plays elevated the experience to a ten. Friday is a great game!

RATING: 8
Fun solo deck builder.  Quick play and engaging, but starts to feel repetitive after a while.  You kind of have to follow the same strategy each game (thinning out bad cards while trying to keep your life points up), but there is a ton of game to game variability in setup and the luck of the draw. I recommend as a solitaire game to absolutely anyone, especially for the price.

What am I doing? Deck building, or deck thinning? I do remember sitting on my office floor playing this game, excitedly losing and trying again, and then again, and it occurred to me as I lost a bit of enthusiasm each time that I was never going to enjoy this, as it was pretty much going to play the same way every time, with the exact same "thin your deck early" strategy. RATING: 6.5
I don't really have a lot of solitaire games to compare this one to, besides cooperative games. I can say, the art is to cartoony and corny for me, and the theme is average at best. The gameplay is solid. I am not sure that this game will have a lot of replay-ability though. The second problem with this game is that it outstays its welcome. Each game takes me about 45 minutes, or more, to play and I am moving at a decent pace. This time is with me usually losing about 3/4s of the way through. The theme, art, and even gameplay is not worth 45 minutes. It would be much better at 25 minutes. I see how the box says 25 minutes. I'm not saying this is a bad game, I'm just saying that for it's length I would probably just rather play Legendary, Flash Point, or Pandemic solo instead of this one most of the time. Still a nice addition to the collection that will get a couple plays most months. Its one of those games you sit in front of the TV and a watch some football for a few hours and play two leisure games of. ***

RATING: 4
First game was fine, second even better, thirds was fun - but then it always felt samey. I'm not a big fan of solitaire games, but there are some which I enjoy (check Shadi Torbey's stuff, "Onirim" and the rest). This one became boring after several games, to the point I just don't think I will every play it again.

You start with a horrible deck of cards and try to trim it by intentionally loosing encounters. There are some decisions involved - when to give up and when to draw more cards at the expense of life points - but for me, it became automatic. Sold it!

RATING: 10
Wow.

When you overcome a hazard, you gain a valuable skill (fight card). When you fail, you lose health, but also learn from your mistakes (rid yourself of bad cards)

The gameplay has choices with consequences, with an excellent deck-building mechanic.

 3 epochs and a boss level provide a rich and satisfying experience.

RATING: 8
After a lucky first win and then getting thrashed a couple of times, I started to get to grips with helping RC to survive. I am not a gamer who searches for the strongest strategy in any sort of methodical way and I like that Friday supports intuitive play, where most of the time I just go with my gut instinct, while avoiding stupid decisions. On this level the game is fairly winnable but still reasonably challenging. 

So yes, for me it's a fun play. The theme is cleverly intergrated and reasonably immersive. A couple of games easily clock in at less than an hour. If this sounds like you, give it a go and also check out "Lord of the Rings - The Adventure Deck Game", which is another solitaire that is mildly challenging and similarly fun. I know I'll be entertained by both these games for years to come.

RATING: 9
Who ever thought losing so often would be so enjoyable ... wait what?

I've lost each game I've played and for some reason I just keep coming back.  Each time I get a little better at it and I know it's possible to win.  It's like a puzzle almost.

[b]Pros:[/b]
- Brilliantly designed cards and boards 
- - SUPER clever use of space and design to make the cards not only easy to read and distinguish but also allow for dual purposed cards. 
- - Cards are easily sorted back out once a game is over.
- - Boards show symbolically what you do with their corresponding decks.

- Really clever mechanics 
- - Escalating difficulty.  Robinson ages each time his deck runs out (getting another bad card) and a new difficulty phase begins each time the hazard deck runs out.
- - Purposely lose at a hazard to 'learn from it' and get rid of bad cards.  Or get cards with the 'destroy' ability to allow you to weed out bad cards on the fly.
- - Special abilities on cards allow you to make some pretty cool combos

- Losing multiple times does not detract from the experience.  It merely makes me want to play more to refine my techniques.

- Scalable difficulty overall; once you've 'mastered' Level 1, there are several more levels of difficulty to try.

- Great for travel:  Small footprint and small storage.  Easy to take anywhere.  No noisy components.

[b]Cons:[/b]
- If you do not like losing a lot, this might not be the game for you.  Losing frequently when first learning the game is common.

- No sleeves available.  If you are a sleeve fiend, there are currently no sleeves available for these.  They're out of print and there is only one maker who has sleeves for them since they are an odd size.  However, this is not necessarily bad.  Since the cards are white/grey core and white-ish bordered, they do not show any obvious marking even after many play-throughts of the game.  I can riffle-shuffle them to my heart's content and not care too much about getting dings on the edges.  It just would have been nice with sleeves since those help when shuffling smaller decks.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Direkt rákerestem, és ahogy a BGG helyezések mutatják, azt kell mondjam, kifejezetten csak és kizárólag solitaire játékot alkotni művészet!
Eléggé egy "elfajzott" dolog ez, elsősorban wargame műfajban találni ilyen játékokat. Azt gondolom, hogy a Friday egy igazán egyedi, és különleges darab, a fentiek pedig csak megerősítenek ebben.
A játék megvalósítását tekintve azonban lehetne kiválóbb is (gondolok itt arra, hogy talán nem kellett volna teljesen egyedi, "nyújtott" kártyaméretet használni, illetve, hogy létezik ennél jobb minőség is - miért nem műanyag lapok???). Ezeket az apróságokat leszámítva viszont nagyon jól elszórakoztat az egész. A Robinson kerettörténet többé-kevésbé illik is az egészhez (igaz, hogy a végén miért kell kalózokkal harcolni az rejtély).
Aranyos egy darab, Friese mesternek sikerült egy igazán egyedi dolgot alkotnia. Javaslom, hogy mindenki próbálja ki, még akár az lelhet benne szépséget, aki idegenkedik a solitaire-ektől.
A szerencse szerepe koránt sem nevezhető elhanyagolhatónak, de hát ez természetes velejárója annak, ha az ember egy lakatlan szigetre vetődik ;) Előny ezzel szemben a gyors setup és a 15-20 perces, rövid játékidő (szemben mondjuk egy normál társas egyszemélyes variációjával).

RATING: 8.5
This game is amazing. A solo deckbuilder that plays in about a half hour and offers incredibly difficult choices. It's so good the way it penalizes you for drawing more cards, both by giving up precious life points, and then ultimately by drawing aging cards. The tough part is that you may need to draw more cards to defeat the hazard, which will then turn into a GREAT card for you. Do you burn through your deck quickly just in the hopes of getting that valuable 4 strength attack card, but take an aging card and lose a couple life points in the process??? These decisions are not simple or obvious in any way. This game is amazing.

RATING: 8
It took me long to like Friday. After the first two sessions I was about to rank it 5, but I decided to give it a few more tries. That has been a good decision. Friday is fantastic solo card game. It comes in a small box, has minimal setup time, plays in 15 - 30 minutes (I am sure that experienced gamers can play it in 10 minutes), and doesn't get boring. The decisions to make are not obvious but not too complicated either. It is a mixture between skill (craft and optimize your deck) and luck (card draws).

Perfect for a quick solo play.

When I am having more time, I will go for a round of Mage Knight.

Btw, Inception is another fine solo card game. And it is PnP.

RATING: 8
For a solo game this is a very good effort. Decisions right at the beginning are a bit obvious, but then get more and more challenging as you progress. It's quite tricky and the game is good that way because after many plays it's not getting boring because it's a challenge. After a couple of games you do sort of work out the better way to play, yet it remains enjoyable as something to play that's light and easy with regular tense moments where you wait to see if the right card will turn up. I'd really like to see this as an iOS application so I could play it again and again while travelling because it also happens to be rather addictive. Nice small box and low price for a good game make it a real winner. I've played it happily as a cooperative game with my eight year old and playing that way helps if you're feeling a bit dubious about the whole solo game experience as it becomes a cooperative experience.

RATING: 7
Fun at first but once you find a strategy that works is comes down to implementing the strategy with little decision making. My strategy is go for the expensive cards. Use them to get free draws to clean out the garbage cards. If a card is not won with the free draws in the first round, let it go, maybe draw one or two more to get rid of more garbage cards. You then have enough points to easily get any card in the later rounds. After figuring this out, that game is pretty mechanical.

RATING: 8
You are cast as Robinson Crusoe, struggling to survive on a tropical island. When you encounter a hazard, such as wild animals or cannibals, you use the cards in your hand to combat it. If you succeed, the hazard card goes into your discard pile and become available to you after the next shuffle; that's pretty standard deck-building fare. But in a clever twist, you can also improve your deck by losing to hazards, because it is then that you can remove bad cards from your deck entirely.

Thematically, you get stronger as you overcome challenges, and you "learn from your mistakes" when you fail. Very clever, and quite addicting. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.5
"[b][thing=43570]Friday[/thing][/b]" is a really slick deck-building designed by [person=141]Friedemann Friese[/person] (yep, the same guy that created "[thing=2651]Power Grid[/thing]").  I've played "[thing=36218]Dominion[/thing]" quite a bit with my gaming friends, but the novelty started waring off pretty quickly after playing other deck-building games such as "[thing=53953]Thunderstone[/thing]," "[thing=69789]Ascension: Chronicle of the Godslayer[/thing]," and "[thing=68425]Eminent Domain[/thing]."  I grew tired of sitting around the table and more or less playing a multi-person solitaire game.  After all, if I wanted to play a solitaire game, then I should just do that on my own when nobody else was available to play, right?  Okay, there's more to those other games and it's not that I dislike deck-building games, but I'd rather use the time with other people to play a more interactive game.  However, "Friday" is an excellent way to scratch the deck-building itch by myself.  This game is packed full of strategy and theme and is another game that's [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/video/13965/friday/]easy to learn[/url], but REALLY difficult to win!

RATING: 7
Friday is a very interesting take on deckbuilding and one of the best combinations of mechanisms and theme that I have ever seen. The game forces you to make some tough decisions about how to improve your deck and manage your food. It takes a few games to get the hang of  how to play optimally, but once you do, it's quite enjoyable. Ultimately, the game suffers from being too easy to predict once you understand how it works. By the time I hit the last level of difficulty, I pretty much did the same things every game with luck being the primary factor in whether I won or lost.

RATING: 7
Friday is an interesting take on deck building.  In this solo you are helping Friday, who was marooned on a dessert Island. You have a small deck of starting cards that have a fighting value and maybe some special ability.  You have to fight through progressively more difficult challenges all the while adding cards to your deck.  As you pass challenges, you add the card to your deck which makes the deck better.  Oh you can fail challenges too, which makes you lose life, but you also get to cull your deck of crappy cards.  

All in all it is a fun little card game I can play while watching a football game or some such.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Friday is a highly addictive little solo game. The theme is very thin - despite having read Robinson Crusoe several times as a boy, I feel no immersion whatsoever. The appeal is strictly from the delight found in solving difficult little problems.

There are 4 levels in the published rules, with apparently minuscule changes from one to the next, but in practice you find that the game truly is that finely tuned. There is also a 5th level, suggested by the designer, where you start with 2 fewer life levels than at level 4. I played 30 games before reaching the point where I needed that challenge. I don't see any end to the replay value, because it will always be possible to remove another life or two as necessary. So far I've won with every number of starting life going down to 13, but hit the wall at 12.

I am normally into more complex games, and more thematic games, but this one drew me in. I'm glad it did, and recommend that others give it a try as well.

Update: I've reached 100 plays. Considering how many games I own, and how many options that gives me, I think 100 plays speaks for itself. This game is special, no mistake.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
An amazingly big game in a small box. Very cleverly designed. I know the art has some detractors, but I quite like it; it's silly, fun, and it fits the theme. I'll be playing this one a lot.

RATING: 8
Superb, elegant, and surprisingly thematic solo deckbuilding game with marvellous artwork.

Each turn you draw hazard cards, which require a certain amount of time/effort to get past, represented by a number of cards to draw from your Robinson deck. If you defeat the hazard (drawing cards equal to its difficulty), you learn some new survival skill, rotate the hazard 180 degrees and add it to your Robinson cards. If not, you suffer a little but can unlearn your weak habits and thin your deck of useless cards. Each time through the Robinson deck makes you age a little more (painful aging cards); each time through the hazards ups the difficulty, until finally you face the pirate attack. Just try not to die.

Luck of the draw plays a factor, but so does skill and strategy. Of course nothing compares to a real opponent, but Friday wrings more fun out of random card draws than I would have thought possible. It's an addictive little gem that, like A Few Acres of Snow, puts all of those tedious Dominion derivatives to shame.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Great solo-game, its hard to win level is surpassed by its fun factor. Each game the player has to adequately address the scarce resources he/she has and try to adequately manage the hazards the game presents in each turn. Lots of re-playability and continuos strategies and tacticts makes this game a must-have.

RATING: 7
[RGG 11 edition] {Adventure; deck-building} Friday is a fun little game.  This is surprisingly challenge for me.  As a solo game, I think this is more fun than Mage Knight and Le Havre (at least with much simpler set up).

The strategy is easy, as all other deck-building games.  You have to get useful cards, and destroyed bad cards.

Most of the tension comes from the ageing cards, which would cause you trouble at the wrong time.  The hazard cards, on the other hand, are not as sexy / dangerous, esp. if one can collect most useful cards at first two phases.  The final showdown with pirates directs the card collection strategy.

The card illustration and the tokens are fun and cute.

Replayabiltiy is average.  Not a keeper in the long run.

RATING: 5
Clever but limited solitaire deck building game. The idea is to successfully negate a number of hazards (depicted by cards) with your existing deck of cards. Once beaten the hazards become part of your deck thereby strengthening it. The hazard deck has to be beaten three times at which point you can attempt to win the game by defeating two pirate cards with your deck. This is a challenging game in many ways and you have to make good decisions on whether to be successful in acquiring hazard cards or not as you try to build your deck most effectively (it tends to be advisable to go for the stronger cards first as they become increasingly difficult to defeat as the game continues). A nice touch is that once you've exhausted your deck, before you reshuffle, you add an ageing card which will negatively impact your deck. The game does scale in difficulty based on your skills as a play but once you've played this a few times you're unlikely to see a lot of variety in the way the game pans out.

RATING: 4.5
Meh. I'm not sure why the designer calls this Friday, when the story doesn't remotely reflect the Robinson Crusoe narrative. And why is the player a territorial and misplaced "Friday" facilitator instead of just Robinson Crusoe?  This gripe wouldn't really matter, but I do think this disconnect mirrors the chief problem of the game, which is that it has no depth and is wholly numerical.

Never once did I feel any sense of adventure or place in this game, where I got progressively better as I learned to better count cards and weigh the odds of garnering requisite numbers.  So basically this is like a regular playing card game (poker or blackjack or solitaire) with some special abilities, some goofy artwork, and zero world building. It's hard to imagine players even bothering the read the one word flavor text after a game or two--it's simply lifeless ornamentation.

I am a fan adventure fiction, the Robinson Crusoe novel, and solitaire adventure games (Perdition's Mouth, Mage Knight, Warhammer Quest ACG, Citadel of Blood, etc.), but by the fourth game of "Solitaire: The Numerical Card Game (with Pictures)," I realized that I would be giving this thing away. Too themeless and numerical to even be a gateway game, but perhaps thrilling for the Dominion crowd (though that at least broke ground for better games).  Time wouldn't pass faster for any castaway stuck with this.

RATING: 7.6
Really enjoying this wonderful little press-yr-luck deck-builder.  The thematic setting is solid and helps build the suspense during some of the tougher decisions.  Am I ready to go after these cannibals now or should I bide my time and scout the island to build experience? Not sure if the long-term replayabiity is there, but after a dozen or so plays, I feel I'm still getting deeper into the system.  There is real strategy here.    

I may rate 'Friday' even higher in the near future...  as I'm getting the feeling that this is *the* solitaire card game that I was hoping Onirim would be. Maybe even better than 'Loyang'.

2/22/13 - Fun little solo game. I recommend anybody who wants a quick-playing solo game to add to their collection pick this one up.

::UPDATE:: 9/26/13
I still think the game is a fine piece of gaming design. However, I've decided it takes a bit too long for what it delivers. It's also pretty cumbersome in the final few turns. The cards really start to pile up and it gets a bit frustrating counting and recounting all the card effects. Then it gets even more complicated when you start tapping the cards you've used, etc.

Still good. I just grew tired of it quickly because the the things above.
