RATING: 7
[thing=43570][/thing] is a solo game with a little of push your luck aspect, but mainly a deck building aspect. In the game you are Friday, trying to teach Robinson to survive the dangers of the island while also wanting that the castaway leaves the island as soon as possible, so you can get your life back.

The way this happens is: every turn, you reveal two hazard cards and choose one of them to face. The hazard cards has a number to be beaten depending on the phase (green, yellow or red) of the game. The cards also has a number of free cards you can reveal from your deck. The cards in your deck has numbers on them - in the beginning of the game (for level 1), they are 2, 1, 0 and -1. Most of them are 0 and -1, so even a challenge of 1 can be difficult early on - Robinson is [i]really[/i] bad at doing stuff. You can pay with life, 1 for 1, to draw more cards. If you beat the hazard, you take the hazard card into your deck, and now it will serve as knowledge (half of the card is the hazard, the other half is the knowledge part), and this cards are much more useful to Robinson than the ones he starts the game. If Robinson fails to beat the hazard, you must pay in life to reach the difficulty number (so, if the number to reach is 2, and you got -1, you must pay 3 life). But this can be a good thing, almost a necessity, since when you pay life to get rid of a hazard, you can also get rid of cards - for every 1 life you pay, you can trash one of the cards revealed to face the hazard. This is how you can get rid of that 0 and -1 cards.

Everytime your deck is depleted and you must reveal a card, you shuffle the cards adding to the deck one aging card. These aging cards are really bad - going from simple -2 to -5 numbers, but some have other effects - cancelling the card with the highest number, stoping the free cards received by the hazard card, and so on. You must pay 2 life to get rid of them (so, if you paid 3 life to avoid a hazard, you can take out a revealed aging card plus one other normal card).

After the hazard deck ends three times (one for each phase), Robinson must face the pirates, represented by two cards that he must face one after the other. If the defeats both, he can leave the island and Friday is finally free to rest. If Robinson fails or dies, technically Friday is also free to rest, but he will probably fell a little bad about the whole thing.

Anyway, [thing=43570][/thing] is a great solo game, that plays rather quick (around 30 min) and offers a lot of choices to be made in such a small frame of time. I enjoyed it completely, well, except for one part: the damn card size! The cards are longer than normal USA size, but have the same width. The artwork is good, like a Robinson Crusoe graphic novel for kids.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
No idea how to rate this. There isn't that much here. You can play it a lot of times until you learn the most reliable ways to beat it. Reminiscent of a puzzle in that way, and I don't like games to be puzzles.

I can't complain about what [i]is[/i] in the game, except for the rule where if you run out of cards during the boss fight you just autolose instead of being able to reshuffle discards like every other time in the game. I'm just not sure how I can be responsible for how many cards I have left when I'm often desperately drawing as many cards as possible just to try to stay alive.

I got this game wanting to see how the mechanics worked. The deck-building thing is kind of interesting in that having a card in your deck isn't necessarily good even if it doesn't, strictly speaking, do anything bad. The dual purpose hazard cards, which when defeated become abilities, could easily be rethemed as monsters and loot. A slick way to simulate an adventurer leveling up as he defeats monsters.

But, the mechanic for getting rid of unwanted cards doesn't seem to make much thematic sense. It's weird to be able to choose to throw a fight, in order to get rid of weaknesses.

...I think this is my only deckbuilding game and I'm pretty sure I will never like this mechanic. I'm OCD about shuffling thoroughly and I don't like that I can't easily visualize what I currently have.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
It seems that there's a specific way to approach this game -- go for the higher-difficulty cards early and save the lower-difficulty cards for later times through the deck -- but I wouldn't say I've mastered the game, so it's hard to say if that's a prevailing way to play.  It's a neat take on the deck-building idea, though it doesn't feel too much like a deck-builder, either.  It has a nice tension, as well as a significant "One more time" feel to it, but I wonder if I would be interested in playing it more once I won it.  The turns seem to be very self-determining (which is a characteristic of most deck-builders), but the fun part is applying your special abilities the right way and knowing when to spend your life points to draw more cards, or lose a fight to get rid of cards you don't want any more.  It's not a bad way to pass the time, since the game takes less than a half-hour to play once you know the flow of the game.

12 plays: 1 player

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
Wow. It has been a while that a game completely blew me away like this one. All the excitement that I felt when I discovered the elegance of deckbuilders came back to me while genuinely being enthralled in the solo experience. The last couple of games I played do not even get close to this one.

Even more, at its heart this is a card counting, push-your-lack game. And I hate both these mechanics. But here the betting really adds to the thrill and the counting is doable by any first grader.

The amazing aspect of Friday is that it gets the balance of discarding and hoarding cards just right. The difficult decision is in eliminating cards despite the fact that they seem valuable. Your deck needs to have both engine-building elements (e.g. draw more cards) and powerful "hit points", and the balance needs to be adjusted to the overall game state.

Brilliant. Elegant. Addictive. Simple but deep. Evolving and full of interesting choices. Amazing. Amazing. Amazing.

RATING: 6
Friday is a tremendously clever solitaire game that uses some of the principles found in deck-builders and collectible card games to deliver an excellent puzzle solving experience. The only caveat I have to a full blown recommendation is that the play deck only consists of about 60 cards, so once you figure out how best to solve the puzzle the game may lose some of your interest. It's only a 15-20 dollar investment though, so by the time that happens most people will probably have already gotten their money's worth.

Finally beat it!

Level 1 = 85 points
Level 2 = 57 points

RATING: 8
This is a really cool one. A singularly solo adventure? And a deck builder?? Leave it to Friedemann Friese to create one of the strangest games I've ever seen or played, but man, what an adventure! Solid mechanics and a very unique take on deck building, this one is a must have for its low price point and for its solo nature, if that's your kind of deal. I love the ideas present here, and the art is silly but enhances the narrative that's being told through the game mechanics. Do you take the hit or go for the lesser evil? What you left behind will be coming back for you later so watch out! So cool.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
First impression:  This is a very dynamic deckbuilding game, which like [thing=11][/thing] has an ever-changing deck, based on what is pulled out of play.  The deck of challenges you face is increasingly thinned as you cull the good cards for "your" deck, but the faster you cycle through that deck, the faster the difficulty rises, and the sooner you have to face pirates.  Stripping your deck down to a lean machine means you cycle through it faster, and each iteration adds a horrific Aging Card to your deck.  Fascinating stuff.

Upon further play: Choosing your combos, and gauging your odds really make this very cleverly designed game.
